{layout:"default",data:[{featuredPost:[{id:Y,title:Z,slug:_,feature_image:$,featured:d,published_at:aa,custom_excerpt:a,html:ab,tags:[{id:k,name:g,slug:i,description:l,feature_image:a,visibility:b,og_image:a,og_title:a,og_description:a,twitter_image:a,twitter_title:a,twitter_description:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a,codeinjection_head:a,codeinjection_foot:a,canonical_url:a,accent_color:a},{id:e,name:f,slug:c,description:a,feature_image:a,visibility:b,og_image:a,og_title:a,og_description:a,twitter_image:a,twitter_title:a,twitter_description:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a,codeinjection_head:a,codeinjection_foot:a,canonical_url:a,accent_color:a}],authors:[{id:H,name:I,slug:J,profile_image:K,cover_image:a,bio:L,website:a,location:a,facebook:a,twitter:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a},{id:N,name:O,slug:P,profile_image:Q,cover_image:a,bio:R,website:a,location:a,facebook:a,twitter:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a},{id:y,name:z,slug:A,profile_image:B,cover_image:a,bio:a,website:a,location:a,facebook:a,twitter:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a}],excerpt:ac,reading_time:S,url:ad}],topPost:[{id:at,title:au,slug:av,feature_image:aw,featured:d,published_at:ax,custom_excerpt:a,plaintext:"June 9 Update:\n\nThe oldest sample we were able to track until now (e69b50d1d58056fc770c88c514af9a82) shows the malware during its early development stage. Dated 2023-04-12, it looks like a Stage 2 sample with the C&C address set to 127.0.0.1, which leads us to believe that it was used for testing. It also includes limited functionality that currently is available in Stage 3 samples (only listening for OS commands (executed with  exec) ), which reinforces our assumption that the malware was in development at that time.\n\nWe also noticed that the Java package was named differently back in April ( dev.sirlennox.nekoclient  instead of  dev.neko.nekoclient).\n\nWe also identified several executables (NekoInstaller\u002FNekoService), as described below:\n\n * NekoInstaller contains a Portable Executable file named NekoServices; at execution it drops the executable file in  C:\\Program Files\\nekoservice\\ServiceHost.exe  and adds it as a service named  NekoService  to run;\n * NekoService contains a JAR file as a resource; it will download a JRE and run the JAR file; the JAR file is then dropped in  C:\\Program Files\\nekoservice\\service.jar\n * the JAR file seems to be a Stage 2 sample\n * the MZ header compilation time for most of these samples ranges between 2023-04-20 18:20:06 and 2023-05-01 22:17:25, and just one sample was identified to be compiled on 2023-05-21 07:58:12, which means that the malware was in development in that timeframe.\n * Based on this evidence, it seems that the attackers initially planned to distribute EXE files rather than JAR ones, but we were unable to assess whether the EXE files have been disseminated in the wild or not.\n\nInitial article:\n\nSeveral Minecraft mods and plugins hosted on the CurseForge and Bukkit modding communities have been tainted with a multi-stage, multi-platform infostealer malware called Fractureiser, a preliminary investigation shows.\n\nSeveral CurseForge and Bukkit accounts have been compromised and used to publish malware-rigged updates of mods and plugins without the knowledge of the original author. These mods have trickled downstream into popular modpacks that have been downloaded several million times to date.\n\nThe malware has 4 stages, labeled 0 through 3. Stage 0 is considered the modified mod or plugin to include obfuscated code that connects to http:\u002F\u002F85.217.144.130:8080\u002Fdl to download the Stage 1 malware.\n\nThe Stage 1 malware comes in the form of a dl.jar file with a SHA-1 sum of dc43c4685c3f47808ac207d1667cc1eb915b2d82. The Stage 1 malware includes a mutex to prevent it from running multiple times, and it seems responsible for infecting other JAR files, establishing persistence and contacting the command and control server in preparation of Stage 2 deployment.\n\nStage 2 (lib.jar or libWebGL64.jar) acts as a downloader and updater for the final payload in Stage 3.\n\nStage 3 brings the final payload, in the form of a jar file that includes a native binary named hook.dll. Hook.dll is exposing two functionalities that are called from Java code: retrieveClipboardFiles - to retrieve file descriptors from the clipboard, used for the virtual machine escape technique (detailed below), as well as retrieveMSACredentials to retrieve Microsoft Live credentials.\n\n\nWhat we know so far\n\nThe first sample apparently dates all the way back to April 24th 2023 in the form of a Stage 0 malware with the 0e583c572ad823330b9e34d871fcc2df hash. The first JAR (Java Archive) file lacks many of the features currently in the malware.\n\nThe malware currently affects Linux and Windows Minecraft installs and attempts to inject itself into all other eligible .jar files on the system, including those that are not part of a Minecraft mod. The malware has a complex logic to determine whether a .jar file is a candidate for infection. Upon modification of the file, the infection code also disables code signing for Java files by removing the META-INF\u002FCERTIFIC.RSA, META-INF\u002FCERTIFIC.EC, META-INF\u002FCERT.SF and META-INF\u002FCERTIFIC.SF\n\nThe malware monitors the clipboard for crypto-currency wallet addresses, then swaps them with the attacker’s to hijack transactions. It also steals Minecraft and Discord authentication tokens, as well as cookies and login data stored in the most popular browsers.\n\nDuring our analysis, we identified interesting behavior we believe is aimed at mod or plugin developers. It looks like the Stage 3 malware targets Windows Sandbox instances used for testing mods by monitoring and constantly poisoning the clipboard in an attempt to infect the host. This behavior is isolated to Windows Sandbox, as it is the only virtualization environment that allows alteration of the host clipboard contents when the virtual machine is running in the background.\n\nWe were able to confirm that dozens of mods and plugins have been rigged with the malware. The affected mods are listed in the Indicators of Compromise section below.\n\nThe overwhelming majority of victims are in the US. We are monitoring the individual components of this malware and will update the threat distribution accordingly.\n\n\nMitigation\n\nBitdefender identifies the malicious code in all stages of execution as Trojan.Java.Fractureiser.*. If you have downloaded any of the infected mods in recent months or have any concern about the integrity of your .jar files, run a deep scan with your favorite security solution such as Bitdefender Total Security.\n\n\nIndicators of compromise\n\nFiles\n\n\n\n\nSHA-1\nDetection\n\n\n\n\n2db855a7f40c015f8c9ca7cbab69e1f1aafa210b\nTrojan.Java.Fractureiser.B, devices have become increasingly popular in recent years, and for good reason. Portable, frequently updated and relatively inexpensive when compared to a new smart TV, these devices offer a convenient, cost-effective, and customizable way to access a vast selection of content from the comfort of your own home. Smart TVs and streaming devices account for a whopping 20% [pdf] of all connected IoT devices, and potential vulnerabilities in firmware could affect a significant user base.\n\nAs the creator of the world’s first smart home cybersecurity hub, Bitdefender regularly audits popular IoT hardware for vulnerabilities that might affect customers if left unaddressed. This research paper is part of a broader program and aims to shed light on the security of the world’s best-sellers in the IoT space. This report covers the Amazon Fire TV Stick and the Insignia\nFireOS TV products. The research discloses vulnerabilities affecting the following products and versions:\n\n * Insignia TV with FireOS versions before 6.2.9.5\n * Fire TV Stick 3rd gen. with FireOS versions before 7.6.3.3\n\nNote: the vulnerabilities presented in this report have been responsibly disclosed to the vendor through their Bug Bounty program. Amazon has released fixes for these issues on Fire TV devices and the Fire TV remote app, and the company has no evidence that this issue has been used against customers. Bitdefender has been working closely with the Amazon Fire TV team through all stages of vulnerability disclosure. We would like to extend our thanks for the prompt response time, communication, transparency and escalation.\n\n\nVulnerabilities at a glance\n\n * Unauthorized authentication through local network PIN brute forcing. This vulnerability was caused by improper implementation of the Password Authenticated Key Exchange by Juggling (or J-PAKE) protocol that could have resulted in attackers gaining control of the device. (CVE-2023-1385)\n * A vulnerability in the setMediaSource function on the amzn.thin.pl service allowed for arbitrary Javascript code to be executed. It could be used to load arbitrary HTTP URLs in the webview. (CVE-2023-1384)\n * A vulnerability in the exchangeDeviceServices function on the amzn.dmgr service allowed an attacker to register services that are only locally accessible. (CVE-2023-1383)\n\n\nDisclosure timeline\n\n\n * Dec 16, 2022 - Bitdefender researchers submit the findings to the bug bounty program\n * Dec 19, 2022: Bug bounty program submits the report for vendor to review\n * Dec 20, 2022: Amazon team acknowledges the findings and starts an internal investigation\n * Apr 12, 2023: Amazon delivers the fix to the public\n * Apr 13, 2023: A bounty is awarded for the findings\n * May 2, 2023: This report is published as part of the coordinated disclosure\n\nDownload the research paper\n\n\nBest practices for IoT devices\n\nHome users should closely monitor IoT devices and isolate them as much as possible from the local network. This can be done by setting up a dedicated network exclusively for IoT devices.\n\nAdditionally, IoT users can use the free Bitdefender Smart Home Scanner app to scan for connected devices, identify and highlight vulnerable ones. IoT device owners should also make sure that they check for newer firmware and update devices as soon as the vendor releases new versions.\n\nTo minimize risks of compromise, smart home users should VPN solutions have witnessed explosive growth in the past few years. These ubiquitous utilities help users keep their internet traffic private, surf anonymously, and bypass restrictions or censorship. And, while most of the world takes this technology for granted,  users in specific regions - such as the people in Iran - have to try out dozens of apps before they find one that is (still) able to bypass ISP restrictions. And, while some VPNs are fake [here is a guide on how to spot a fake VPN app] or blocked, some others are deliberately laced with malware.\n\nContext\n\nDuring routine analysis of detection performance, we noticed a batch of processes that respected the same pattern in the process names. These names begin with sys, win or lib followed by a word that describes the functionality, such as bus, crt, temp, cache, init, and end in 32.exe. We later noticed that the .bat files and the downloaded payloads respect the same naming convention. Further investigation revealed the components are part of a monitoring application called SecondEye, developed in Iran and distributed legitimately via the developer’s website. We also found that some spyware components were already described in an article published by Blackpoint. In the article, researchers drew attention to the dangers of legally distributed monitoring software with malicious behavior.\n\nOur own researchers, as well as Blackpoint’s, found the campaigns used components of the SecondEye suite and their infrastructure. However, these components were not delivered through a legitimate SecondEye installer but rather through Trojanized installers of VPN software (also developed in Iran) that dropped the spyware components along with the VPN product.\n\nAttack at a glance\n\n * Bitdefender has discovered a malware campaign that uses components of SecondEye - a legitimate monitoring application - to spy on users of 20Speed VPN, an Iranian-based VPN service, via trojanized installers.\n * EyeSpy has the ability to fully compromise online privacy via keylogging and stealing of sensitive information, such as documents, images, crypto-wallets, and passwords.\n * The campaign started in May 2022, but detections peaked in August and September. Most of these detections originate from Iran, with a small pool of victims in Germany and the US.\n\nIndicators of Compromise\n\nAn up-to-date, complete list of indicators of compromise is available to Bitdefender Advanced Threat Intelligence users. 2014, Bitdefender IoT researchers have been looking into the world's most popular IoT devices, hunting for vulnerabilities and undocumented attack avenues. This report documents four vulnerabilities affecting devices powered by the ThroughTek Kalay Platform. Due to the platform’s massive presence in IoT integrations, these flaws have a significant downstream impact on several vendors.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIn the interconnected landscape of the Internet of Things (IoT), the reliability and security of devices, infrastructure and data are paramount. Among the many frameworks facilitating the operation of IoT devices, ThroughTek's Kalay platform stands as a linchpin, powering \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.throughtek.com\u002Fadvantages\u002F\"\u003Emore than 100 million devices worldwide\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. With a predominant presence in surveillance cameras and security devices, ThroughTek Kalay's influence underscores its significance in safeguarding homes, businesses, and integrators alike.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003ENOTE: the vulnerabilities presented in this paper have been responsibly disclosed to the affected vendors. Specific firmware information is available in each report below. We would like to extend our thanks to the involved vendors for their prompt acknowledgement of vulnerability and rapid patch release.\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"timeline\"\u003E\u003Cem\u003ETimeline\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EOct 19, 2023: Bitdefender contacts ThroghTek and sends the vulnerability report.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EOct 20, 2023: Vendor confirms the issues.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EOct 26, 2023: Vendor asks for over 90-day time extension to implement and deploy the fix.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EMar 15, 2024: Additional extension is requested.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EApr 12, 2024: Coordinated vulnerability disclosure is scheduled for May 15 2024 to allow all affected parties to apply the patches\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EApr 16, 2024: Vendor confirms that all affected SDK versions have been patched.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EMay 15, 2024: This report becomes public.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"vulnerabilities-exposed\"\u003EVulnerabilities Exposed\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6321\"\u003ECVE-2023-6321\u003C\u002Fa\u003E allows an authenticated user to run system commands as the root user leading to the full compromise of the device.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6322\"\u003ECVE-2023-6322\u003C\u002Fa\u003E  enables attackers to gain root access through a stack-based buffer overflow vulnerability in the handler of an IOCTL message, typically employed in configuring motion detection zones in cameras. This is a vulnerability specific to some devices that use motion detection features.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6323\"\u003ECVE-2023-6323\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, for instance, exposes a loophole wherein a local attacker can illicitly obtain the AuthKey secret, effectively helping an attacker establish a preliminary connection to the victim device.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003ELastly, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6324\"\u003ECVE-2023-6324 \u003C\u002Fa\u003Eexploits a vulnerability allowing attackers to infer the pre-shared key for a DTLS session, a critical prerequisite for connecting and talking to the victim devices.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWhen chained together, these vulnerabilities facilitate unauthorized root access from within the local network, as well as remote* code execution to completely subvert the victim device.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E*Remote code execution is only possible after the device has been probed from the local network.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"affected-vendors\"\u003EAffected vendors\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWhile these vulnerabilities affect the TUTK platform and subsequently impact most implementations, our research was conducted on three major devices sold worldwide. Given that some vendors had device-specific vulnerabilities, individual timelines are available in each report.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"owlet-cam-v1-and-v2\"\u003EOwlet Cam v1 and v2\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003EOwlet Cam uses the ThroughTek Kalay solution to communicate with clients over the Internet.  The three vulnerabilities (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6323\"\u003ECVE-2023-6323\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6324\"\u003ECVE-2023-6324\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6321\"\u003ECVE-2023-6321\u003C\u002Fa\u003E) can be chained together to allow an attacker to obtain root access from the local network and then to execute commands on the device. On Owlet Cam, command execution is obtained via \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6321\"\u003ECVE-2023-6321\u003C\u002Fa\u003E - a vulnerability in IOCTL message 0x6008E, which is used to unpack archives containing OTA updates.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EA technical dive into the vulnerabilities and how they are daisy-chained to compromise the Owlet Cam is available below:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C!--kg-card-begin: html--\u003E\u003Cp align=\"center\"\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Ffiles\u002F2024\u002F05\u002FBitdefender-PReport-owlet-7745.pdf\" class=\"button-view-all d-inline-block\"\u003EDownload the whitepaper\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C!--kg-card-end: html--\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"wyze-cam-v3\"\u003EWyze Cam v3\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBitdefender researchers have identified three vulnerabilities in Wyze Cam v3. They are tracked as CVE-\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6322\"\u003E2023-6322\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6323\"\u003ECVE-2023-6323\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6324\"\u003ECVE-2023-6324\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Chained together, these vulnerabilities allow an attacker to obtain root access from the local network. In this case, command execution on the Wyze Cam v3 is obtained via \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6322\"\u003ECVE-2023-6322\u003C\u002Fa\u003E - a stack-based buffer overflow vulnerability in the handler of IOCTL message 0x284C that is used to set the motion detection zone.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EA technical dive into the vulnerabilities and how they are daisy-chained to compromise the Wyze Cam v3 is available below:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C!--kg-card-begin: html--\u003E\u003Cp align=\"center\"\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Ffiles\u002F2024\u002F05\u002FBitdefender-PReport-Wyze-7745.pdf\" class=\"button-view-all d-inline-block\"\u003EDownload the whitepaper\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C!--kg-card-end: html--\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"roku-indoor-camera-se\"\u003ERoku Indoor Camera SE\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe vulnerabilities in the Roku Indoor Camera SE are identical to those in Wyze Cam v3 (and potentially other security cameras). Bitdefender researchers have daisy-chained CVE-\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6322\"\u003E2023-6322\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6323\"\u003ECVE-2023-6323\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6324\"\u003ECVE-2023-6324\u003C\u002Fa\u003Eto obtain the necessary prerequisites for talking to the camera and for running OS commands as root user.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EA technical dive into the vulnerabilities and how they are daisy-chained to compromise the Roku Indoor Camera SE is available below:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C!--kg-card-begin: html--\u003E\u003Cp align=\"center\"\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Ffiles\u002F2024\u002F05\u002FBitdefender-PReport-roku-7745.pdf\" class=\"button-view-all d-inline-block\"\u003EDownload the whitepaper\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C!--kg-card-end: html--\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"implications-and-remediation\"\u003EImplications and Remediation:\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe ramifications of these vulnerabilities extend far beyond the realm of theoretical exploits, as they directly impact on the privacy and safety of users relying on devices powered by ThroughTek Kalay. Our findings have been responsibly disclosed both to the platform vendor, as well as to the tested integrators. Updated versions of firmware and SDKs have been made available for the impacted devices to prevent these issues from being exploited in real-life scenarios.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E",authors:[{id:s,name:t,slug:u,profile_image:v,cover_image:a,bio:w,website:a,location:a,facebook:a,twitter:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a}],tags:[{id:C,name:D,slug:E,description:a,feature_image:a,visibility:b,og_image:a,og_title:a,og_description:a,twitter_image:a,twitter_title:a,twitter_description:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a,codeinjection_head:a,codeinjection_foot:a,canonical_url:a,accent_color:a},{id:e,name:f,slug:c,description:a,feature_image:a,visibility:b,og_image:a,og_title:a,og_description:a,twitter_image:a,twitter_title:a,twitter_description:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a,codeinjection_head:a,codeinjection_foot:a,canonical_url:a,accent_color:a},{id:m,name:n,slug:o,description:a,feature_image:a,visibility:p,og_image:a,og_title:a,og_description:a,twitter_image:a,twitter_title:a,twitter_description:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a,codeinjection_head:a,codeinjection_foot:a,canonical_url:a,accent_color:a}],excerpt:"Since 2014, Bitdefender IoT researchers have been looking into the world's most popular IoT devices, hunting for vulnerabilities and undocumented attack avenues. This report documents four vulnerabilities affecting devices powered by the ThroughTek Kalay Platform. Due to the platform’s massive presence in IoT integrations, these flaws have a significant downstream impact on several vendors.\n\nIn the interconnected landscape of the Internet of Things (IoT), the reliability and security of devices,",reading_time:3,url:"\u002Fblog\u002Flabs\u002Fnotes-on-throughtek-kalay-vulnerabilities-and-their-impact\u002F"},{id:"66d5c3d2d0ec1aefc7d722ce",title:"Vulnerabilities Identified in LG WebOS",slug:"vulnerabilities-identified-in-lg-webos",feature_image:"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F04\u002Fweb-4869856_1920.jpg",featured:d,published_at:"2024-04-09T16:00:00.000+03:00",custom_excerpt:a,html:"\u003Cp\u003EAs the creator of the world’s first smart home cybersecurity hub, Bitdefender regularly audits popular IoT hardware for vulnerabilities. This research paper is part of a broader program that aims to shed light on the security of the world’s best-sellers in the IoT space. This report covers vulnerabilities discovered while researching the LG WebOS TV operating system.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWe have found several issues affecting WebOS versions 4 through 7 running on LG TVs. These vulnerabilities let us gain root access on the TV after bypassing the authorization mechanism. Although the vulnerable service is intended for LAN access only, Shodan, the search engine for Internet-connected devices, identified over 91,000 devices that \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.shodan.io\u002Fsearch?query=product%3A%22LG+webOs+TV%22\"\u003Eexpose this service to the Internet\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F04\u002Fimage-1.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"392\" height=\"206\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"vulnerabilities-at-a-glance\"\u003EVulnerabilities at a glance\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EBitdefender researchers discovered a vulnerability that lets an attacker bypass the authorization mechanism in WebOS versions 4 through 7. By setting a variable, the attacker can add an extra user to the TV set (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6317\"\u003ECVE-2023-6317)\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EAnother vulnerability allows attackers to elevate the access they gained in the first step to root and fully take over the device (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6318\"\u003ECVE-2023-6318\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EA third vulnerability (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6319\"\u003ECVE-2023-6319\u003C\u002Fa\u003E) allows operating system command injection by manipulating a library responsible with showing music lyrics.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-6320\"\u003ECVE-2023-6320\u003C\u002Fa\u003E vulnerability lets an attacker inject authenticated commands by manipulating the \u003Ccode\u003Ecom.webos.service.connectionmanager\u002Ftv\u002FsetVlanStaticAddress\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003EAPI endpoint.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"vulnerable-os-versions\"\u003EVulnerable OS versions\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EwebOS 4.9.7 - 5.30.40 running on LG43UM7000PLA\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EwebOS 5.5.0 - 04.50.51 running on OLED55CXPUA\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EwebOS 6.3.3-442 (kisscurl-kinglake) - 03.36.50 running on OLED48C1PUB\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EwebOS 7.3.1-43 (mullet-mebin) - 03.33.85 running on OLED55A23LA\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"disclosure-timeline\"\u003EDisclosure timeline\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003ENovember 01, 2023: Vendor disclosure\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003ENovember 15, 2023: Vendor confirms the vulnerabilities.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EDecember 14, 2023: Vendor requests extension\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EMarch 22, 2024: Patch release\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EApril 09, 2024: Public release of this report\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"a-technical-look-into-the-discovered-vulnerabilities\"\u003EA technical look into the discovered vulnerabilities\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWebOS runs a service on ports 3000\u002F3001 (HTTP\u002FHTTPS\u002FWSS) which is used by the LG ThinkQ smartphone app to control the TV. To set up the app, the user must enter a PIN code into the display on the TV screen. An error in the account handler lets an attacker skip the PIN verification entirely and create a privileged user profile.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F04\u002FPicture-1.jpg\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"880\" height=\"660\" srcset=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw600\u002F2024\u002F04\u002FPicture-1.jpg 600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F04\u002FPicture-1.jpg 880w\" sizes=\"(min-width: 720px) 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe function that handles account registration requests uses a variable called \u003Cstrong\u003EskipPrompt\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E which is set to true when either the \u003Ccode\u003Eclient-key\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E or the \u003Ccode\u003Ecompanion-client-key\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E parameters correspond to an existing profile. It also takes into consideration what permissions are requested when deciding whether to prompt the user for a PIN, as confirmation is not required in some cases.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWe can request the creation of an account with no permissions, which will be automatically granted. Then we request another account with elevated permissions, but we specify the \u003Ccode\u003Ecompanion-client-key\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Evariable to match the key we got when we created the first account. The server will confirm that this key exists but will not verify if it belongs to the correct account. Thus, the \u003Cstrong\u003EskipPrompt\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E variable will be true and the account will be created without requesting a PIN confirmation on the TV.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThis vulnerability, identified as CVE-2023-6317, has been confirmed to affect webOS 4.9.7, 5.5.0, 6.3.3-442, and 7.3.1-43.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EHaving created a privileged account without user interaction, we now have access to a large attack surface that was inaccessible before. We have found two authenticated command injection vulnerabilities that lead to root access, and another that runs commands as the dbus user.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"authenticated-command-injection-in-the-processanalyticsreport-method-from-the-comwebosservicecloudupload-service\"\u003EAuthenticated command injection in the processAnalyticsReport method from the com.webos.service.cloudupload service\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe \u003Ccode\u003EprocessAnalyticsReport\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E method requires three parameters: \u003Ccode\u003Etype\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, \u003Ccode\u003EreportFile\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, and \u003Ccode\u003EoriginalFile\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. When the \u003Ccode\u003Etype\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eparameter is set to \u003Ccode\u003Eanalytic\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E the \u003Ccode\u003EreportFile\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eparameter will be passed to a system command without being sanitized.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAlthough requests to this method cannot be performed directly, we can use another endpoint, \u003Cem\u003Esystem.notifications\u002FcreateAlert\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, to bypass this restriction, accessible only to authenticated users who have the \u003Ccode\u003EWRITE_NOTIFICATION_TOAST\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E permission. The \u003Cem\u003Eonclose \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eparameter supported by this endpoint allows us to perform internal requests to services that are not exposed, similar to SSRF. After we create the notification, we trigger the \u003Cem\u003Eonclose \u003C\u002Fem\u003Ecall through the \u003Ccode\u003Esystem.notifications\u002FcloseAlert\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E endpoint, performing the request to the vulnerable endpoint.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe specified file must exist on the device, but we can bypass this constraint by using the \u003Cem\u003Edownload \u003C\u002Fem\u003Emethod from the \u003Cstrong\u003Ecom.webos.service.downloadmanager \u003C\u002Fstrong\u003Eservice, which will create a file in the \u003Ccode\u003E\u002Fmedia\u002Finternal\u002Fdownloads\u002F\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E directory with an arbitrary filename. Both the \u003Ccode\u003EprocessAnalyticsReport\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eand download\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Emethods can be accessed through the \u003Ccode\u003EcreateAlert\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eendpoint.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe vulnerable command is created on line 83 and executed on line 84:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F04\u002FPicture-2.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"526\" height=\"198\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThis vulnerability, identified as CVE-2023-6318, has been confirmed to affect webOS 5.5.0, 6.3.3-442, and 7.3.1-43.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"authenticated-command-injection-in-the-getaudiometadata-method-from-the-comwebosserviceattachedstoragemanager-service\"\u003EAuthenticated command injection in the getAudioMetadata method from the com.webos.service.attachedstoragemanager service\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe \u003Cem\u003EgetAudioMetadata \u003C\u002Fem\u003Emethod requires two parameters: \u003Ccode\u003EdeviceId\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E and \u003Ccode\u003EfullPath\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. While the \u003Cem\u003EdeviceId \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eparameter is not important, the \u003Cem\u003EfullPath \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eparameter will be passed, under certain conditions, to a system command without being sanitized. If this parameter points to a file with the \u003Cem\u003E.mp3\u003C\u002Fem\u003E extension the service will search in the same directory for the corresponding lyrics file with the same name (\u003Cem\u003E.lrc\u003C\u002Fem\u003E extension). If found, the first four bytes of the lyrics file will be compared with the sequence \u003Ccode\u003E\\xFF\\xFE\\x00\\x00\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. If they match (meaning that the file is UTF1632 encoded) the service will try to decode it using the \u003Cem\u003Eiconv\u003C\u002Fem\u003E binary. This binary will be called together with the full filename without prior sanitization, leading to command injection.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBoth the .mp3 and .lrc files must exist on the device and can be created using the \u003Ccode\u003Edownload\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Emethod mentioned earlier. All required methods can be accessed through the \u003Ccode\u003EcreateAlert\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E endpoint.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe vulnerable code in \u003Cem\u003EconvLrcStringByBinary \u003C\u002Fem\u003Efrom the \u003Cem\u003Easm \u003C\u002Fem\u003Ebinary:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F04\u002FPicture-3.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"550\" height=\"36\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThis vulnerability, identified as CVE-2023-6319, has been confirmed to affect webOS 4.9.7, 5.5.0, 6.3.3-442, and 7.3.1-43.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"authenticated-command-injection-in-the-comwebosserviceconnectionmanagertvsetvlanstaticaddress-endpoint-allows-execution-of-commands-on-the-device-as-dbus\"\u003EAuthenticated command injection in the com.webos.service.connectionmanager\u002Ftv\u002FsetVlanStaticAddress endpoint allows execution of commands on the device as dbus\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe \u003Ccode\u003EsetVlanStaticAddress\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eendpoint requires three parameters: \u003Ccode\u003Eip_address\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, \u003Ccode\u003Ebcast_address\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E, and \u003Ccode\u003Enetmask\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E. All threeparameters will be passed to a system command without being sanitized. Before calling this endpoint, we must first call the \u003Ccode\u003EcreateVirtualLan\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003Cem\u003E \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eendpoint. These endpoints require the \u003Ccode\u003EREAD_NETWORK_STATE\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E permission.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAlthough the user that executes the commands is \u003Cem\u003Edbus\u003C\u002Fem\u003E, this account has similar permissions as the \u003Cem\u003Eroot \u003C\u002Fem\u003Euser.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EVulnerable code in \u003Ccode\u003Ehandle_set_vlan_static_address_command\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E from \u003Ccode\u003Elibwca2.so\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E library:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F04\u002FPicture-4.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"834\" height=\"90\" srcset=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw600\u002F2024\u002F04\u002FPicture-4.png 600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F04\u002FPicture-4.png 834w\" sizes=\"(min-width: 720px) 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThis vulnerability, identified as CVE-2023-6320, has been confirmed to affect webOS 5.5.0 and 6.3.3-442.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003ENote: LG has fixed the reportred issues prior to the publication of this research. The LG Product Security Response Center(PSRC) security advisories for the reported vulnerabilities \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Flgsecurity.lge.com\u002Fbulletins\u002Ftv#updateDetails\"\u003Eare available here\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.  LG has also released automatic and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.lg.com\u002Fus\u002Fsupport\u002Fsoftware-firmware-drivers\"\u003Emanual updates\u003C\u002Fa\u003E for the affected firmware versions and ve advise that vulnerable TV set model owners take action immediately.\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E",authors:[{id:s,name:t,slug:u,profile_image:v,cover_image:a,bio:w,website:a,location:a,facebook:a,twitter:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a}],tags:[{id:C,name:D,slug:E,description:a,feature_image:a,visibility:b,og_image:a,og_title:a,og_description:a,twitter_image:a,twitter_title:a,twitter_description:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a,codeinjection_head:a,codeinjection_foot:a,canonical_url:a,accent_color:a},{id:e,name:f,slug:c,description:a,feature_image:a,visibility:b,og_image:a,og_title:a,og_description:a,twitter_image:a,twitter_title:a,twitter_description:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a,codeinjection_head:a,codeinjection_foot:a,canonical_url:a,accent_color:a},{id:m,name:n,slug:o,description:a,feature_image:a,visibility:p,og_image:a,og_title:a,og_description:a,twitter_image:a,twitter_title:a,twitter_description:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a,codeinjection_head:a,codeinjection_foot:a,canonical_url:a,accent_color:a}],excerpt:"As the creator of the world’s first smart home cybersecurity hub, Bitdefender regularly audits popular IoT hardware for vulnerabilities. This report covers vulnerabilities discovered while researching the LG WebOS TV operating system.\n\nWe have found several issues affecting WebOS versions 4 through 7 running on LG TVs. These vulnerabilities let us gain root acces",reading_time:bF,url:"\u002Fblog\u002Flabs\u002Fvulnerabilities-identified-in-lg-webos\u002F"},{id:"66d5c3d2d0ec1aefc7d722c5",title:"Vulnerabilities identified in Bosch BCC100 Thermostat",slug:"vulnerabilities-identified-in-bosch-bcc100-thermostat",feature_image:"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F01\u002Ftechnology-gbbc352657_1920.jpg",featured:d,published_at:"2024-01-11T17:26:30.000+03:00",custom_excerpt:a,html:"\u003Cp\u003ESeveral factors underscore the importance of smart thermostats: energy efficiency, environmental sustainability, and the spread of smart home technologies. These devices have a major impact on energy conservation and its associated cost savings, while making homes noticeably more comfortable.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThis combination of energy efficiency, convenience and environmental consciousness, which resonate with the current priorities of individuals, governments and societies, have led to the diversification of an ecosystem comprised of multiple vendors and technologies.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAs the creator of the world’s first smart home cybersecurity hub, Bitdefender regularly audits popular IoT hardware for vulnerabilities that might affect customers if left unaddressed. This research article is part of a broader program and aims to shed light on the security of the world’s best-sellers in the IoT space. This report covers the Bosch BCC100 thermostat and reveals vulnerabilities affecting the SW version 1.7.0 – HD Version 4.13.22.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch1 id=\"vulnerability-at-a-glance\"\u003EVulnerability at a glance\u003C\u002Fh1\u003E\u003Cp\u003E[LOCAL] During our security audit, Bitdefender researchers discovered a vulnerability that lets an attacker on the same network replace the device firmware with a rogue version (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cve.org\u002FCVERecord?id=CVE-2023-49722\"\u003ECVE-2023-49722\u003C\u002Fa\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch1 id=\"disclosure-timeline\"\u003EDisclosure timeline\u003C\u002Fh1\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EAug 29, 2023: Bitdefender makes first contact with the vulnerable vendor and submits the full report\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003ESep 18, 2023: Bitdefender learns that the issue is still undergoing internal investigation at the vendor\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EOct 04, 2023: Vulnerability is triaged and confirmed.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EOct 30, 2023: Bitdefender asks for an update, and is told the issue is still being handled\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003ENov 11, 2023: Fix deployed in production.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003ENov 17, 2023: Bitdefender asks for additional info about the update timeline in preparation for coordinated vulnerability disclosure\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EJan 11, 2024: This report becomes public.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch1 id=\"vulnerability-walkthrough\"\u003EVulnerability walkthrough\u003C\u002Fh1\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe thermostat has two microcontrollers that work together, as seen in the picture below. The one on the right, in yellow, is a Hi-Flying chip, HF-LPT230, that implements the Wi-Fi functionality. It acts as a network gateway for the logic microcontroller. The STMicroelectronics chip, STM32F103, in red, is the brain of the device and implements the main logic.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"blob:https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002F2e5782fb-b912-4ffd-b093-f5ee73f84c9e\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe STM chip has no networking capabilities and instead relies on the Wi-Fi chip to communicate with the Internet. It uses the UART protocol to pass data to the Wi-Fi chip, which acts as a gateway\u002Fproxy and establishes the actual connection to the servers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWe have discovered that the Wi-Fi chip also listens on TCP port 8899 on the \u003Ca\u003ELAN, and\u003C\u002Fa\u003E will mirror any message received on that port directly to the main microcontroller, through the UART data bus. This means that, if formatted correctly, the microcontroller can’t distinguish malicious messages from genuine ones sent by the cloud server. This allows an attacker to send commands to the thermostat, including writing \u003Ca\u003Ea malicious\u003C\u002Fa\u003E update to the device.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"updating-the-thermostat-with-arbitrary-firmware\"\u003EUpdating the thermostat with arbitrary firmware\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe thermostat communicates with the \u003Cstrong\u003Econnect.boschconnectedcontrol.com\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E server through JSON encoded payloads over a \u003Ca\u003Ewebsocket\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. The packets sent by the server are unmasked, making them easy to imitate.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EFirst, we send the “device\u002Fupdate” command on port 8899 that lets the device know that there is a new update and to start the update procedure:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E\u003Ca\u003E\\x81\\x46{\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\"cmd\":\"device\u002Fupdate\",\"device_id\":\"&lt;device mac address&gt;\",\"timestamp\":1111111}\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThis will prompt the thermostat to ask the cloud server for details about the update:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E{\"cmd\":\"server\u002Ffireware\",\"device_id\":\"&lt;device mac address&gt;\",\"timestamp\":\"&lt;unix timestamp&gt;\",\"model\":\"BCC101\",\"version\":\"1.7.0\",\"id\":\"0\"}\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EEven though the server responds with an error code because there is no update available:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E{\"error_code\":\"99\",\"cmd\":\"server\u002Ffireware\",\"device_id\":\"&lt;device mac address&gt;\",\"timestamp\":\"&lt;unix timestamp&gt;\"}\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe device will also accept a forged response containing the update details:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E\\x81\\x7e\\x01\\x33{\"error_code\":\"0\",\"cmd\":\"server\u002Ffireware\",\"device_id\":\"&lt;device mac&gt;\",\"timestamp\":\"&lt;unix timestamp&gt;\",\"model\":\"BCC101\",\"version\":\"&lt;fw version&gt;\",\"url\":\"&lt;firmware URL&gt;\",\"size\":\"&lt;firmware size&gt;\",\"isize\":\"0\",\"pic_pos\":\"2930\",\"md5\":\"&lt;firmware md5&gt;\",\"type\":0,\"release_date\":\"1111-11-11\"}\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThis packet contains the URL where the firmware will be downloaded from, the size and MD5 checksum of the firmware file, and the version of the new firmware, which must be higher than the current one. There are no validation mechanisms for firmware update authenticity.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIf all the conditions match, the thermostat asks the cloud server to download the firmware and send it through the websocket:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Ccode\u003E{\"cmd\":\"server\u002FdeviceUpdate\",\"device_id\":\"&lt;device mac&gt;\",\"timestamp\":\"&lt;unix timestamp&gt;\",\"url\":\"&lt;firmware URL&gt;\",\"pindex\":\"0\"}\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe URL must be Internet-accessible, as the cloud server is the component that downloads the file. After the device receives the \u003Ca\u003Efile\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, it performs the upgrade. At this point, the device is considered totally compromised.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"blob:https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002F9d5ad958-a94e-4603-8a32-481a6b580793\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"best-practices-for-iot-devices\"\u003EBest practices for IoT devices\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EHome users should closely monitor IoT devices and isolate them as completely as possible from the local network. This can be done by setting up a dedicated network exclusively for IoT devices.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAdditionally, IoT users can use the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.bitdefender.com\u002Fsolutions\u002Fhome-scanner.html\"\u003Efree Bitdefender Smart Home Scanner\u003C\u002Fa\u003E app to scan for connected devices, identify and highlight vulnerable ones. IoT device owners should also check for newer firmware and update devices as soon as the vendor releases new versions.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003ETo minimize risks of compromise, smart home users should consider adopting a network cybersecurity solution integrated into the router, such as the NETGEAR Orbi or Nighthawk routers powered by \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.netgear.com\u002Fhome\u002Fservices\u002Farmor\u002F\"\u003EBitdefender Armor\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E",authors:[{id:s,name:t,slug:u,profile_image:v,cover_image:a,bio:w,website:a,location:a,facebook:a,twitter:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a}],tags:[{id:e,name:f,slug:c,description:a,feature_image:a,visibility:b,og_image:a,og_title:a,og_description:a,twitter_image:a,twitter_title:a,twitter_description:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a,codeinjection_head:a,codeinjection_foot:a,canonical_url:a,accent_color:a},{id:C,name:D,slug:E,description:a,feature_image:a,visibility:b,og_image:a,og_title:a,og_description:a,twitter_image:a,twitter_title:a,twitter_description:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a,codeinjection_head:a,codeinjection_foot:a,canonical_url:a,accent_color:a},{id:m,name:n,slug:o,description:a,feature_image:a,visibility:p,og_image:a,og_title:a,og_description:a,twitter_image:a,twitter_title:a,twitter_description:a,meta_title:a,meta_description:a,codeinjection_head:a,codeinjection_foot:a,canonical_url:a,accent_color:a}],excerpt:"Several factors underscore the importance of smart thermostats: energy efficiency, environmental sustainability, and the spread of smart home technologies. Dive on Supplement Scams: How AI Drives ‘Miracle Cures’ and Sponsored Health-Related Scams on Social Media",slug:"deep-dive-on-supplement-scams-how-ai-drives-miracle-cures-and-sponsored-health-related-scams-on-social-media",feature_image:"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Fpexels-pixabay-161688.jpg",featured:d,published_at:"2024-07-10T16:00:00.000+03:00",custom_excerpt:a,html:"\u003Cp\u003ESponsored social media content has become increasingly present on feeds. Sponsored ads can often be beneficial as they are customized to suit online personas, offering relevant content tailored specifically for you. While personalized ads can help enhance your online experience, not all are legitimate. In fact, scams originating from phony ads on social media have increased dramatically, with potentially severe consequences for consumers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"sponsored-supplement-scams-on-social-media-platforms\"\u003ESponsored supplement scams on social media platforms\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EHealth and well-being are favored topics cybercriminals use in their campaigns to steal information and dupe people out of money.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThese scams involve criminals creating fake ads and websites that offer low-cost miracle products, medication, or treatments that promise to cure persistent conditions, even cancer.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EResearchers at Bitdefender Labs collected and analyzed health related scams across the globe over a three-month period from March-May 2024.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EKey Findings\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EA marked increase of health-related fraudulent ads leveraging AI-generated images, videos and audio promoting various supplements on Meta’s social platforms: Facebook, Messenger and Instagram\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe highest number of followers of a compromised\u002Ffake page that promoted false advertisements is over 350,000\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EScammers used over 1,000 different deepfake videos across communities\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EOver 40 medical supplements ads were promoted\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EMost of the ads cater to targeted geographical regions with tailored content using the names of celebrities, politicians, TV presenters, doctors and other healthcare professionals to bait consumers\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EImpersonated figures include Brad Pitt, Cristiano Ronaldo, George Clooney, Dr. Ben Carson, Bill Maher, Denzel Washington, Dr. Heinz Lüscher, Dr. Jan Šula, Dr. Roman Šmucler, Dr. Marko Noč, Dr. Tomaž Klokočovnik, Dr. Fekete Andrea, among others\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EImpersonated figures in Romania include Andreea Esca, Dr. Mihail Pautov, Dr. Monica Pop and many others. A boosted sponsored advertisement impersonating a well-known Romanian priest gathered over 6000 reactions and 900 shares\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003ECampaigns targeted millions of recipients across the globe including Europe, North America, the Middle East, Asia, and Australia.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"socially-engineered-deepfakes-are-changing-the-landscape\"\u003ESocially engineered deepfakes are changing the landscape\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EToday's technological advancements, including AI, allow scammers to significantly increase the reach and success rate of their fraudulent activities, making it much harder for individuals and organizations to defend against them. In the context of health scams, such as the ones we describe in our report below, the rise of deepfakes grants fraudsters a fresh take on old schemes and more credibility than ever before.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EHere’s why:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EAI allows threat actors to tailor scam messages and ads to the interest and vulnerabilities (health problems) of individuals, and as such increases the likelihood of engagement with fraudulent content\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EIt enables scammers to generate highly convincing messages that are both grammatically correct and in context with the ads they push through social media platforms\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003ETailored ads associated with fake videos of celebrity figures and well-known medical professionals further increase the likelihood of a successful scam campaign\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe analyzed deepfake samples are of all possible qualities. While most of the videos show clear signs of tampering, our researchers found many instances of videos that were more difficult to put down in the deepfake category.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAll samples use the same technique, adapted to each targeted audience --use the credibility and fame of a well-known figure to promote easy cures for common ailments in the targeted group. We have observed deepfakes in the following languages: English (which include audiences from the US, UK, Australia and so on), Romanian, Italian, Spanish, Portuguese, German, French, Russian, Czech, Slovak, Slovene, Latvian, Lithuanian, Hungarian, Bulgarian, Polish, Greek, Croatian and others.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"the-phenomenon-in-numbers\"\u003EThe phenomenon in numbers\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWhile it may seem that the supplement scams just changed means of propagation, the fact that millions of people can be reached by paying modest sums is extremely alarming and needs urgent moderation. Here are some statistics that prove how dangerous this phenomenon has become:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThousands of pages promoting medical supplement scams\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003ETens of thousands of social media advertisements created by the actors behind the campaign\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"cybercriminals-cheat-users-out-of-money-time-and-health\"\u003ECybercriminals cheat users out of money, time and health\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EMalicious actors utilize various strategies to strengthen their credibility and deceive social media users. Here are some of the most used tactics:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EScammers will say anything to convince you to buy their fake products and services. They include catchy phrases designed to captivate and manipulate emotions\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003ERush individuals into deciding on the spot with limited time offers and discounts. Although they initially bait individuals with a discount for purchasing a single product, the scammers are extremely insistent over the phone trying to convince you to purchase multiple products at once to ensure that the “treatment” will be effective.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003ESpread false promises to exploit vulnerable individuals in need\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EUse deepfake technology to make convincing but entirely fabricated content. These methods are all part of a concerted effort to deceive and manipulate targets for their purposes.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cp\u003EDespite the often too-good-to-be-true nature of such advertisements, many individuals still fall prey to this deceptive content. This can be attributed to several factors, including a lack of awareness, blind trust in online information, the prevalence of false reviews, and the need for individuals to regain their health. In some cases, the scammers even exploit individuals who are desperate in finding a solution or treatment that will help them ease symptoms or even cure chronic underlying diseases.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESome of the most observed scenarios are depicted in the following examples, sourced from advertisements in Romania and around the globe:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E1. Advertisements are described as alternatives to conventional medicine. The decline in trust in conventional medicine, aggravated by many scandals within the pharmaceutical industry, is often used to prompt consumers into seeking alternative solutions.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg Using deepfake technology to impersonate well-known medical practitioners or respected figures in the medical field. For example, many ads claim their product is endorsed by influential physicians like \"Doctor [X]” or “TV personality [X],” particularly in regions where these specialists are well known. To boost credibility, scammers use deepfake technology to create videos of these individuals who give a “scientific” explanation for the effectiveness of the products.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EImages or videos of seniors aiming to evoke empathy are also used to endorse bogus health products, specifically if they are related to any geriatric illnesses.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg False promises. 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E4. Persuasive messages. Examples of such messages include phrases like \"limited stock,\" \"act now or lose,” \"promotion only today\" or claims that it's a \"secret remedy the pharmaceutical industry or doctors don’t want you to know.\" This may make people act out of pressure or hurry, without carefully inspecting the details.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Fscam_gr_blurred.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1209\" height=\"807\" srcset=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw600\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Fscam_gr_blurred.png 600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw1000\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Fscam_gr_blurred.png 1000w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Fscam_gr_blurred.png 1209w\" sizes=\"(min-width: 720px) 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Fdx_blurred.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"983\" height=\"541\" srcset=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw600\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Fdx_blurred.png 600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Fdx_blurred.png 983w\" sizes=\"(min-width: 720px) 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E5. Promoted by pages that impersonate medical specialists. This is closely linked to the use of deepfakes for impersonation. Since the advertisement is tied to a respected specialist, victims may be convinced that the medicine will solve their problem.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Fleon_danaila_impers_blurred.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"620\" height=\"611\" srcset=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw600\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Fleon_danaila_impers_blurred.png 600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Fleon_danaila_impers_blurred.png 620w\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Frosemary_galbraith_blurred.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"633\" height=\"526\" srcset=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw600\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Frosemary_galbraith_blurred.png 600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Frosemary_galbraith_blurred.png 633w\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E6. False reviews. They serve to deceive potential victims by creating a facade of legitimacy and positive feedback around the scammer's products or services.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Freviews_2_blurred.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1827\" height=\"856\" srcset=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw600\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Freviews_2_blurred.png 600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw1000\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Freviews_2_blurred.png 1000w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw1600\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Freviews_2_blurred.png 1600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Freviews_2_blurred.png 1827w\" sizes=\"(min-width: 720px) 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Freviews3_blurred.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1848\" height=\"829\" srcset=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw600\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Freviews3_blurred.png 600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw1000\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Freviews3_blurred.png 1000w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw1600\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Freviews3_blurred.png 1600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Freviews3_blurred.png 1848w\" sizes=\"(min-width: 720px) 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"the-anatomy-of-a-supplement-scam-campaign\"\u003EThe anatomy of a supplement scam campaign\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIt all starts with fraudsters crafting social media pages to spread misleading advertisements. Bitdefender Labs researchers have spotted thousands of pages that promote cures for common ailments or health problems.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002FPicture2.jpg\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1100\" height=\"630\" srcset=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw600\u002F2024\u002F07\u002FPicture2.jpg 600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw1000\u002F2024\u002F07\u002FPicture2.jpg 1000w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002FPicture2.jpg 1100w\" sizes=\"(min-width: 720px) 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EHere are some of their most common features:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E· Pages have a modest number of likes or low engagement\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E· The pages have a generic name and give the sense of a trusted organization or health blog\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E· They lack posts or have vague wellness-related content\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThese pages, however, do excel in ads that promote products or supplements in a variety of languages (often by the same page). The ads use flashy images, deepfake videos and bold statements to catch the attention of the audience. The campaigns are well coordinated, with ads set to target specific countries, age groups and even genders. While so-called diabetes cures are not gender specific, beauty products and male performance enhancers are. The perps behind these campaigns even tweak their ads to reach a wide audience by targeting the specific needs of potentially vulnerable customers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EMost of the ads lead to a website promoting a health product along with a limited discount, fake reviews (presumably generated by LLMs) and fake conversation prompts with “specialists” that give potential customers the idea of a personalized treatment. These websites typically include approvals by trusted individuals from the country of the targeted audience – physicians, influencers, TV personalities and so on. While most of the websites are just poorly designed one-product e-shops, some clone popular news outlets from the targeted country.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ECertain ads even make their way up to well-known media outlets, through paid articles.\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAll website instances share a common goal: maximize product sales using all sorts of marketing techniques including last-minute discounts, low stocks or fortune-based games that offer additional discounts.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EOrders\u002Fpurchases are typically initiated by entering personal data such as the name, email (sometimes required for additional discounts) and phone number. Upon submitting this data, customers are called by an “agent” who immediately asks for additional information to confirm the order. But most importantly, potential customers are told that they need to purchase multiple products to finalize the order, otherwise “the treatment wouldn’t have an effect.”\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003ETrying to purchase a single product for test purposes is impossible, with agents emphasizing that they “respect their clients and want the best results.”\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThey are marketed as miracle supplements that promise to make patients feel better or cure different health problems.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"motivation-behind-online-supplement-peddlers\"\u003EMotivation behind online supplement peddlers\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe supplement business is very profitable, and, unfortunately, it also attracts scammers who use digital tools to spread disinformation and attract unsuspecting customers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe obvious motivation for the people behind these ads is financial, even though most of the promoted websites don’t immediately prompt for financial information but indicate that orders can be made by calling a specific phone number. \u003Cstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe use of deep fakes and the fact that certain products are promoted by hundreds or thousands of pages indicate that these shady promotion practices yield good results. Selling the metaphorical snake oil, while not uncommon, gains a huge audience and perhaps even credibility in the context of modern social media. While conducting this research, we observed thousands of social media pages and websites serving these supplement scams, and we believe that the real numbers are in the tens of thousands.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAnother interesting detail is that the ad infrastructures used easily allow the publishing of such shady content – phrasing, pictures and videos frequently get changed to prevent easy moderation. If any of the pages involved get banned on any given platform, the actors will most likely have hundreds of others that can replace it. Some pages even have thousands of likes, which indicate the fact that scammers might even use stolen pages bought from the dark web, “rebranding” them so they vaguely resemble the topic in discussion.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EVulnerable groups\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe ads are aimed at individuals that might have or think they have certain ailments. In our research, we have observed “medications” for conditions such as diabetes, sight related difficulties, joint pain, heart issues and so on. We have also observed “products” that have “miraculous” anti-aging or other aesthetic effects, and bold claims that guarantee to improve memory or repel Alzheimer’s -- all accompanied by positive testimonials and clinical studies. Most importantly, we’ve regularly noticed the claim that these impressive medical results are backed by extensive studies and approved or recommended by famous or well-known medical practitioners in the targeted community. Thus, the audience is extended to the fanbase of the impersonated trusted individuals.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EAn example of an ad impersonating a well-known physician\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E“Dr. Heinz Lüscher: Incurable joint diseases can be cured in 3 days! Thanks to a simple...”,\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002FPicture3.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1430\" height=\"665\" srcset=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw600\u002F2024\u002F07\u002FPicture3.png 600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw1000\u002F2024\u002F07\u002FPicture3.png 1000w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002FPicture3.png 1430w\" sizes=\"(min-width: 720px) 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EOther recurring topics are alcohol abuse, weight loss, and intimacy-related problems – plenty of ads promise that the products cure the condition in a couple of days.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWhile we cannot fully state that the ads are aimed at the elderly, certain ones are clearly framed in that manner. This ad description for example: “Aos 67 anos, pareço ter 40! Vou mostrar-vos como me livrei das rugas sem Botox.” which roughly translates to “At 67, I look 40! I'm going to show you how I got rid of wrinkles without Botox.”\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Faos_67_anos_blurred.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"1574\" height=\"774\" srcset=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw600\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Faos_67_anos_blurred.png 600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw1000\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Faos_67_anos_blurred.png 1000w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Faos_67_anos_blurred.png 1574w\" sizes=\"(min-width: 720px) 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAnother example clearly targeting the elderly would be “Jak jsem si ve svých 72 letech obnovil klouby - zbavil jsem se invalidity a běhám jako nový člověk!”, which translates to “How I Restored My Joints At 72 - I Got Disabled And I'm Running Like A New Person!”.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002FPicture4.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"624\" height=\"304\" srcset=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw600\u002F2024\u002F07\u002FPicture4.png 600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002FPicture4.png 624w\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThe fact that most analyzed websites allow the order of products via phone also indicates that the target audience might not be accustomed to online orders or payments.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"how-to-identify-supplement-scam-ads\"\u003EHow to identify supplement scam ads\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EMost of the fraudulent ads can be first identified by looking out for these warning signs:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThey promise that a product will help treat or prevent diseases or even cure multiple ones\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe agents use aggressive sales tactics and give you medical advice\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe supplements are endorsed by well-known celebrities or medical practitioners\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe ads rush you into placing an order by citing limited supplies and huge discounts\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EYou cannot purchase a single product and are required to fill out a form or call a number\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe ads have hundreds of positive reviews from satisfied customers. The links on which the product is promoted might also mention spectacular discounts or the unique opportunity to play a luck-based game to gain one (wheel of fortune, what’s behind the door, etc.):\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Fdoors.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"946\" height=\"507\" srcset=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002Fsize\u002Fw600\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Fdoors.png 600w, https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Fdoors.png 946w\" sizes=\"(min-width: 720px) 720px\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cfigure class=\"kg-card kg-image-card\"\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Fimages\u002F2024\u002F07\u002Fwheel_of_fortune.png\" class=\"kg-image\" alt loading=\"lazy\" width=\"430\" height=\"398\"\u003E\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EUse caution when running into this type of messages:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E[person] has revealed the secret about [illness];\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EDoctors\u002Fphysicians are lying about [illness];\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThis natural method has already helped thousands of people in [Country];\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003ESymptoms will disappear in [short amount of time];\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EResults from the first days of using! 100% natural with no adverse effects;\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EIt is time to say goodbye to [illness];\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EAnybody that has [illness] - read this before it gets deleted!\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EPharmacies have tricked us\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"how-to-protect-against-supplement-scams\"\u003EHow to protect against supplement scams\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EFollow the instructions only of a certified physician when it is necessary to use certain medications or medical products. Fake or bogus supplements may pose serious health risks and contain dangerous substances.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EResearch supplement companies and products online before making any purchases or handing out your contact information or credit card. Look for any customers complaints.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EVerify all supplement ads you come across on social media platforms, including Facebook. Be wary of ads using medical jargon. Scammers will use scientific-sounding terms to mislead you into making a purchase. If you are not familiar with the particular brand, talk to your healthcare provider first.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EIf a supplement website still looks credible, one might use tools such as WHOIS to check the domain registration date – if it was registered recently, it is again a reason to ignore and\u002For report the ad.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003ENever pay by debit card and keep a close eye on any credit card statements to check for recurring payments.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EUse a dedicated security solution with anti-phishing and anti-fraud filtering systems to fend off harmful platforms and websites.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"worried-about-scams\"\u003EWorried about scams?\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWhen unsure about an email, online proposal, text or request, you can check it with Bitdefender Scamio on \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fapi.whatsapp.com\u002Fsend?phone=19548585275\"\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EWhatsApp\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E, \u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.messenger.com\u002Ft\u002F102488646283695\"\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EFacebook Messenger\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E, \u003C\u002Fstrong\u003Eor\u003Cstrong\u003E \u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.bitdefender.com\u002Fsolutions\u002Fscamio.html\"\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003Ea web browser\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E for free! since at least 2018.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe actor uses the legitimate RMM, presumably as a backup access point into the victim’s network.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EThe aim of the
