xmlns=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.w3.org\u002F2000\u002Fsvg\" viewBox=\"0 0 24 24\"\u003E\u003Cdefs\u003E\u003Cstyle\u003E.a{fill:none;stroke:currentColor;stroke-linecap:round;stroke-linejoin:round;stroke-width:1.5px;}\u003C\u002Fstyle\u003E\u003C\u002Fdefs\u003E\u003Ctitle\u003Edownload-circle\u003C\u002Ftitle\u003E\u003Cpolyline class=\"a\" points=\"8.25 14.25 12 18 15.75 14.25\"\u002F\u003E\u003Cline class=\"a\" x1=\"12\" y1=\"6.75\" x2=\"12\" y2=\"18\"\u002F\u003E\u003Ccircle class=\"a\" cx=\"12\" cy=\"12\" r=\"11.25\"\u002F\u003E\u003C\u002Fsvg\u003E\n                \u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n            \u003C\u002Fa\u003E\n        \u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n        \u003Col\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EFull Account Takeover\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: The Solarman platform’s \u003Ccode\u003E\u002Foauth2-s\u002Foauth\u002Ftoken\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E API endpoint lets attackers generate authorization tokens for any account. By modifying the JSON payload, attackers can gain control over any regular or business account. This means that a malicious user could iterate through all accounts, take over any of them and modify inverter parameters or change the way the inverter interacts with the grid.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EToken Reuse Across Platforms\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: JWT tokens issued by the Deye Cloud platform are also valid on the Solarman platform, granting full access to the accounts based on their ID. This cross-platform vulnerability can lead to widespread unauthorized access in the absence of well-defined boundaries to isolate vendors.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EExcessive Data Exposure\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: The Solarman platform’s API endpoints return excessive information about organizations, including private details such as email addresses and phone numbers. This information can be harvested to exploit the platform’s users and organizations. In addition to personally identifiable information, an attacker can chain this with the first vulnerability to run subsequent queries on the account and obtain GPS coordinates for solar installations as well as their real-time production capacity.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Fol\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"vulnerabilities-in-the-deye-platform\"\u003EVulnerabilities in the Deye platform\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Col\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EHard-Coded Credentials\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: The Deye platform uses a hard-coded account (`SmartConfigurator@solarmanpv.com` with password \u003Ccode\u003E123456\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E) to access device data. This account can obtain an authorization token that grants access to any device, exposing sensitive information such as software versions, Wi-Fi credentials, and more​ (see the Deye disclosure report available below)​.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EInformation Leakage\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: The API endpoint \u003Ccode\u003E\u002Fuser-s\u002Facc\u002Forgs\u003C\u002Fcode\u003E on eu1.deyecloud.com returns excessive private information about users, including names, email addresses, phone numbers and user IDs. This endpoint can be exploited to leak information about all users on the platform​.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EAuthorization Token Generation\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: The \u003Ccode\u003E\u002Foauth-s\u002Foauth\u002F\u003C\u002Fcode\u003Etoken API endpoint has the same vulnerability as the endpoint used by Solarman. However, the JWT token that is generated contains a wrong value and is not accepted by the server, even though the token is valid and signed. This issue could pose a future risk if not properly patched​.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Fol\u003E\n        \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-card kg-file-card kg-file-card-medium\"\u003E\n            \u003Ca class=\"kg-file-card-container\" href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblogapp.bitdefender.com\u002Flabs\u002Fcontent\u002Ffiles\u002F2024\u002F08\u002FBitdefender-PReport-deye-creat7907.pdf\" title=\"Download\" download\u003E\n                \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-contents\"\u003E\n                    \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-title\"\u003EVulnerabilities in the Deye platform\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n                    \n                    \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-metadata\"\u003E\n                        \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-filename\"\u003EBitdefender-PReport-deye-creat7907.pdf\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n                        \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-filesize\"\u003E2 MB\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n                    \u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n                \u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n                \u003Cdiv class=\"kg-file-card-icon\"\u003E\n                    \u003Csvg xmlns=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.w3.org\u002F2000\u002Fsvg\" viewBox=\"0 0 24 24\"\u003E\u003Cdefs\u003E\u003Cstyle\u003E.a{fill:none;stroke:currentColor;stroke-linecap:round;stroke-linejoin:round;stroke-width:1.5px;}\u003C\u002Fstyle\u003E\u003C\u002Fdefs\u003E\u003Ctitle\u003Edownload-circle\u003C\u002Ftitle\u003E\u003Cpolyline class=\"a\" points=\"8.25 14.25 12 18 15.75 14.25\"\u002F\u003E\u003Cline class=\"a\" x1=\"12\" y1=\"6.75\" x2=\"12\" y2=\"18\"\u002F\u003E\u003Ccircle class=\"a\" cx=\"12\" cy=\"12\" r=\"11.25\"\u002F\u003E\u003C\u002Fsvg\u003E\n                \u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n            \u003C\u002Fa\u003E\n        \u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\n        \u003Ch2 id=\"implications-for-grid-security\"\u003EImplications for Grid Security\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWhile most of our previous findings have a serious impact on the individual or on the internet itself, the flaws detailed in this research are fundamentally different. Access to devices interacting with the grid can have devastating effects on the proper functioning of the grid itself. These vulnerabilities pose a significant threat to grid security in several ways:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EUnauthorized Control\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: Attackers can take over accounts and control solar inverters, disrupting power generation and potentially causing voltage fluctuations.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EData Breaches\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: Sensitive information about users and organizations can be leaked, leading to privacy violations, information harvesting, targeted phishing attacks or other malicious activities.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EOperational Disruptions\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E: By accessing and modifying settings on solar inverters, attackers can cause widespread disruptions in power distribution, impacting grid stability and potentially leading to blackouts.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"disclosure-timeline\"\u003EDisclosure Timeline\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"solarman\"\u003ESolarman:\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EMay 22, 2024: Bitdefender reaches out to Solarman for a security contact\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EMay 23, 2024: Bitdefender gets in touch with Solarman security team and sends vulnerability information\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EMay 24, 2024: Vulnerabilities acknowledged; account takeover gets immediately fixed\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EJun 17, 2024: Vendor confirms that a fix for the API returning too much information is in place.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EJul 17, 2024: Vendor confirms that the Deye token reuse issue is now fixed.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch3 id=\"deye\"\u003EDeye:\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E\u003Cul\u003E\u003Cli\u003EMay 22, 2024: Bitdefender reaches out to Deye for a security contact\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EJun 03, 2024: Authorized security partner asks Bitdefender for details\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EJun 06, 2024: Bitdefender sends the vulnerability report\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EJun 17, 2024: Bitdefender asks for an update on the reported issues\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EJul 09, 2024: Deye sends an overview of the fixed issues\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003Cli\u003EAug 07, 2024: This report becomes public as per the coordinated vulnerability disclosure protocols.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\u003C\u002Ful\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"conclusion\"\u003EConclusion\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIntegrating solar power into the grid offers immense benefits, but it also introduces attack surfaces that equipment makers must take into account. The security flaws found in the Deye and Solarman platforms highlight the need for robust cybersecurity in managing solar energy systems, as well as in general IoT setups.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EProtecting the grid from cyber threats is crucial to ensuring reliable and secure power for all. As we continue to embrace renewable energy, we must also remain vigilant and proactive in securing our energy infrastructure against evolving threats.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWe’d like to thank the vendors involved for acknowledging and fixing these vulnerabilities in a timely manner.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EToo long for a read? Watch this piece of research as a video presentation on August 9 at 5\u003C\u002Fem\u003E:00PM (Creator Stage 2\u003Cem\u003E @ the IoT Village talks) at Defcon. If you are attending Defcon 32 in person, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.iotvillage.org\u002Fdefcon.html\"\u003Ecome see the talk live\u003C\u002Fa\u003E or meet and greet the researchers.\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Ch2 id=\"appendix\"\u003EAppendix\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\u003Cp\u003EHere is a list of Solarman partner companies using the platform and potentially affected by the reported vulnerabilities. Our testing reveals that most of these vendors have scheduled maintentance windows to deploy security patches. We presume that these scheduled maintenance intervals are set to implement mitigations for the issues we reported to Solarman and Deye.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003C!--kg-card-begin:
